## 02 Introduction-To-Lca-Part-A-Why-Lca

Look around you.
How many objects do you have in the
room around you? Each of these objects has
its own supply chain, which is generating
environmental emission in possibly the entire world. In addition, each of this
product will be disposed off and create
additional emission at the end of its life. Crucial that we understand how products are impacting
the world and we need a tool which will work on the whole life cycle of
pro-products and this is where life-cycle
assessment is useful. Today, we'll look and understand
why LCA can be used and how it can be used and what are the main stages covered by LCA. We will, as learning
objective first, list the lifecycle
stages of a product. You will be able to
express the reasons why LCA is needed and then identify some of the
main application of LCA here. If we look at the different
stages of an LCA, everything starts
first in the mining, in the extraction of
metals or energy, where we dig the earth
and take lots of earths, which has a small
amount of resources, and we have to extract and
transform these resources, concentrate them, refine the energy mean in refineries to get the raw material
that we can then use in manufacturing
and assembly here. One, we have manufactured
and assembled product. Many industry, like
a car industry is not producing most
of the components, but it's assembling these
components into a car here. Once we have that, we have to package and
distribute our products. We have the user of
our product here. This product, ones this
have been used once could be either reused, recycled, or being disposed in a landfill, or disposing an incinerator, creating emission using
resources at each of the stage of our life cycle, going from cradle to cradle
to grave or in fact, from cradle to cradle, if we recycle our
different products. Let's look at why LCA
is really needed. It's interesting in the 1990s
we were starting to work on LCA in different
labs in the world. I met with environmental
manager from Jacob Coffee. They had their own
environmental departments. He told me basically, "We have 80 percent of our environmental effort is made indoor in the
wall of my company." That only 20 percent of the environmental impact is
happening where the coffee is manufactured and 80 percent is either created of the impact is either happening upstream, for example, in
agriculture here, or downstream during
the use phase or during the waste treatments. We have this discrepancy
between where we put our environmental efforts and
where we have our impacts, which we need to solve. That's where life-cycle
assessment is enabling us to have this broad view avoiding
to just the place, pollution from one
place to another, or solve one problem
but create another one. We want to be more
integrated there. This development of LCA
has been in parallel with the way environmental has been seen in our pre-1970s. We have really whistleblowers, I mean, Silent Spring Carson, who are environmental
prophets who have the vision that we cannot
continue as we are doing here. Nowadays we see they were right. We have limits, in that case, very few regulation at
that time some concern, but not much waste it's
not so much an issue. 1973, we have an energy
crisis in the world. Price of petrol is
10 times higher in a few months and we
start to realize, we need to do more. We have in 1970s and '80s, emission control,
emission regulation, end of pipe control are coming. Usually, it's limited to an environmental
department in a company. It's not the whole company
which is aiming at that here. A time where environmental
NGOs are opposing industry largely. We have this
conflict industry. Say, we want to
continue to produce, the society needs our product, our chemical and you say no, you cannot do that. There are these also with
the nuclear industry, quite a lot of opposition there. In 1990s, it's interesting. We start here to have a
more proactive era where people start to see possibilities of synergy between
environment and economics. Instead of opposing,
we start saying we might have some
win-win situation. We have new integrated
pollution control or take back strategy, where you have
to produce or to take back the computer
to recycle them. The awareness is go all the sector and organization, and that's where
life-cycle approaches gets further deadlock here, because we need this view going through the
entire supply chain. We entered in 2000 in a more progressive way where actors start to
really collaborate. It was amazing collaboration. We see DuPont collaborating
with NGO, WWF, or even Greenpeace entering
in collaboration with industry with a goal to improve the way we are
managing our chemical, managing of emission, managing our environment
and biodiversity. Here we have integrated
product policy in particular here in
the European Union, which looks not only at what comes out of the chimney
or the industry, but look at the product
with anti perspective thus the generalization
of LCA and use of LCA. This now is integrated, I would say since
the last two years, three years, we start having
these climate action, which in especially
the young generation, has taken off in an
amazing way and change, perhaps not so much
here presently, that change radically the
way the government and the different parliaments are voting laws and progressing, at least in Europe presently. Just to give you an example, how things have changed and how now someone who has a producer, or even a bank, has now extended responsibility compared to where we were
in the last century. In 2000, we were asked
by a local bank, I was working at the
Ecole Polytechnic in Lausanne, Switzerland, and this local bank asks us to do the environmental
footprints, but also the environmental management plans of their bank. We did how much
electricity was used, we collected that, we did the carbon footprint
of the entire bank, but we also studied how
they were investing the money the different
people we're giving them, and what type of
things that were financing with this money. We gave our results to
the board of the bank, the president and all the
board members were there, and one thing we insisted on was that they were financing petroleum trade and transport, but they were not in the
management system assessing the environmental
risk involved and especially checking
the quality of life, the tanker who were
carrying the petrol there. We gave that recommendation, the internal lawyer evaluation
of our work will say, no bank has ever been sued
for financing oil transport so this is not a substantial risk and
they did not act on it. December 2002, a
26-years-old tanker sink on the shore of Spain and really 77,000 metric tons
of heavy fuel. The entire coast, we know with an oil spill, look how
messy it looks like. Unfortunately, this
local bank had finance part of this
transportation of that ship. They made the headline
of the local news. I can tell you, I jump back on my slides to look if
we had communicated clearly that they
should have done and be rigorous on that, and in fact, two months later,
the bank had left this profitable petrol
business because of the risk of image associated
with this transport. Very interesting,
limited risk, no, because we are
expecting things now from a bank that was not
expected 10 years earlier.


## 03 Introduction-To-Lca-Part-B-Uses-Of-Lca

Now, so
lifecycle assessment in this context, in this area of producer responsibility
is used in different way. Using business strategy and R & D that
the two main usage where respondents 60%. Where for each of them it can exceed 100%
because some people are using it for several goals at the same time. It's used in product design, okay? That's an important use. Education. Is used today in education
that's what we are doing. Policy development,
the EU in particular is using quite a bit the LCA approach to adapt
their policy and development. But also in company we
have that happening. Product declaration labeling Aiso
label free level needs kind of LCA or to be accepted and recognized, certified. Sales and
procurement is not negligible but it's it's substantially lower
than in business strategy. So, what type of problem
are we addressing with LCA? It's how to decide priorities. And because the world just cannot
afford to do everything as Barlow who was the head of the International Academy
for Technical Science at that time. Was quoting and saying he had the
engineering view that the problem is not how to tackle, the problem
engineering can solve everything. But what we just cannot afford that. So, we need priority. And in many cases LCA
is there to bring and choose among the different
environmental proposals. Those who are efficient,
those who will bring the maximum benefits for
a minimum investments and improve our worlds an affordable and
efficient way. So, in summary, the main life
cycle stages of a product here, is material extraction first. Then we move to transformation
of the raw material. We have the manufacturing and assembly of
the product, packaging and distribution. Use and reuse and recycling and
finding the disposal. These are all the stage which
need to be accounted for and considered in the product.. In this proactive era,
LCA meet the needs for producer responsibility beyond
its own production sites. And we've seen that there
are multiple types of application by
multiple actors for LCA. So, now to further discover LCA, you will take the second
chapter of our book here. Download the book on on your system and take the second chapter and
just read the case study here. Where we look for

## 01 A-History-Of-Lca-Standards

How old or I should say, how young is
life-cycle assessment as a method than the science? We'll look and recognize that the history of LCA
and LCA standard is relatively recent and has been rapidly evolving and
progressing at the same time. We want you to be able to list
the main LCA standards or LCA-based standards that we
will refer to in this class. A short historical
review of LCA. The first LCA has been done 1969 on beverage
packaging by Coca-Cola. In fact, with a strong
interest in solid waste. And it's interesting that we
started with waste in LCA. Is it because waste is the most important
program in the world? No, probably not. But it's what we see is what is left in our
hands when we've consume our product and
that we don't really need. That's why the focus
started with that. The Swiss EPA produced
several studies on packing material which
were very good basis and starting basis for then
evolve to other studies because they had all
different type of energy production
mostly for packing, or they had all the
different material they had collected the data for. The first restructuring of LCA came through the
SETAC code of practice, a small documents from Peston
workshop with experts. And that was developed by the SETAC Society for Environmental Toxicology
and Chemistry, which is historically
the society who has and continues to develop LCA with conferences bringing
together every year about 200 scientists working on this method
development in the world. This SETAC so then to show the different working
group from 1995-1999, which really led to further structure the method
and serves as a basis for an important milestone which was the first ISO standards
that was determined there. At the end of the 90s, you know scientists
how they are. They like to work together, but they like their own
methods, their own approach. To really arrive to recommendation and help
as a practitioner, we thought we need
an outside partner beyond the scientific
society like SETAC. With my colleague,
we were heading in fact the group on
impact assessment and we thought let's contact the United Nations
Environmental Program UNEP, and to see if they would
collaborate and by chance, when we contacted
them, Kofi Annan, the UN Secretary at that
time had just called for studying on the
environmental impact of the entire supply chain so we were just at the right time. 2002 we launch, with UNEP the
life-cycle initiative which is still continuing and arriving now at what we were
aiming at 20 years ago, which was to arrive to recommending an impact
assessment method. But in between came a
very important progress 2003, the ecoinvent database, which is one of the
largest database or the largest database
with 4,000 processes at the level of unit processes is made available here or
mostly in Switzerland, but with adaptation nowadays
in different countries. In parallel with
the inventory side, we have different impact
assessment method like for toxicity USEstox, ReCiPe is a Dutch method, Impact World+ is our own method developed with the Polytechnique
Montreal in Canada. The effort of the
life-cycle initiative here, which is they've logged
on LCIA guidance, where we had two of these
framing workshop in the last four years and we are aiming at arriving as I say, at the recommended reading
practices and methods. In short, there has been
a lot of progress in terms of data availability
for life-cycle inventory, your life is much simpler than mine when I started LCA to do that and in life cycle
impact assessment, which are available. What are the standard available, which are life-cycle based
or life-cycle related. ISO has a whole series, and this is a 14,000 series
of environmental standards. In fact, relatively
surprising way regarding the newness
of the approach, LCA has been one of the first environmental
management standard here with two standards, 14040, which was principal
and framework, which gives a frame
then which is developed within 14044, which is the one you
want to look if you have really detailed question
or need guidance for that. Though they give guidance, they don't give factors, they don't give number. That's the work in the
life-cycle initiative to provide these more detailed, harmonized method and numbers. But it helps avoiding a
lot of the misuse of LCA. If an LCA is ISO compatible, it ensure basic
quality of the LCA. 2014, a water footprint
is developed, which is really
life-cycle based, headed by one of my former collaborator,
Sebastian Harbor, who had the process
for giving this water footprint
LCA-based approach. Two other standard shortly 14048 is giving some data
documentation and 14049, our example of application for this goal and scope and
the inventory analysis. No ISO standard for carbon footprint but there
is a product life cycle, greenhouse gas accounting
and reporting practice from the World Resources
Institute and the World Business Council
on Sustainable Development. In short, life-cycle assessment, what the feature or
the main feature, it relates the environmental
impact to the product, service, or the function. We've seen with the
popcorn example, how we need to relate
not to just kilogram, but to look at what is a product function and have a unit like the cubic meter use, which is representative of
a function of a backing, which is protecting and
transporting material. With LCA, we quantify
mass balance of emission of resources over the whole life cycle
from cradle to grave, or even cradle to cradle when we have recycling
in our life cycle, and we cover multiple
impacts: greenhouse effect, toxicity resources
that we look at, not only a single aspect, like carbon or water here. We have the four phases of LCA, goal and scope, inventory, impact assessment
interpretation that we will go further in more detail
in the following chapters. In summary, LCA is
relatively recent, but has been rapidly evolving and progressing
and maturing. I would say we are
in a place which is amazing compared to where
we were 30 years ago, leading to standardization and
a large data availability, which may make it
much easier to apply. One of the first tool that
has been standardized, and we have to
recognize a standard only provide a frame
for good practice, but not necessarily the method
or consensus methods that could help making results more consistent
across different LCA, and that are needed to be as a complement to
the ISO standards. Also, we need to be sure
that the quality of data is recognized and
ensured in all LCAs.


## 02 Lca-Compared-To-Other-Environmental-Tools-Part-A

Of course LCA is the best tool
because I've been working for more than 28 years on it but
it's not the only one and we need to acknowledge the other
environmental tool and does understand for
which problem is which tool suited. So let's look at these different tool and
differentiate as learning objectives, the main purpose and characteristics
of LCA and various environmental tools. And second identify the most
appropriate tools for a range of environmental problems. Different tools for different purposes so the first thing is LCA as such is
essentially an environmental tool. To study the supply chain We
have an other tool which are not necessarily environment and
which will be a compliment LCA. And these are life cycle
costing which is a sort of LCA. But focusing on the economic
aspect on the cost side and social LCA will cover the other
pillar of sustainability. So life cycle costing is
studying the economic here and but also with the supply
chain perspective and social LCA will look at like
children labor over the entire supply chain of example
shoe product in that case. But LCA itself by default
is an environmental LCA which study environmental problem. Now LCA itself and on the environmental
side can be complemented by several other quantitative tools which are addressing
different questions and problems. And these are and we'll come back and
look at them in detail, substance and mass flow analysis, risk assessment,
carbon and water footprints. In addition to quantitative
tool we have upstream of LCA. Some more general concept lifecycle
thinking being sort of generalization and qualitative LCA way of addressing problem. Eco design which is
an approach how to design new products which
are environmental friendly and industrial ecology is an approach
where you close the cycle and you use for
example the waste from one industry, you use them as the raw material for
a second industry etc. And you you try to close the different
cycles here on I would say downstream from LCA in terms of application you have
more procedure oriented methods. First environmental impact assessment
which can be partly quantitative. It's not only qualitative or
procedural but it's it's still in the frame of
legal procedure usually. Ecolabel which are qualifying certain products
according to given criteria. Environmental audit of the company
which look at the weak point of the company what is
the stage where they are? And environmental management system
which are tools to systematically include the environmental dimension
in all decision of company. So to look at this further
in further details at the environmental different tools. Let's let's look how decision is taken and
usually decisions are taken by the top management people who are well paid in
the company but they are not on their own. And first they will rely on for
the development of new product. They will rely on engineers
could be material engineer, mechanical engineer depending on
the company and what they are doing. And these people are this engineer
are are really looking at the technological system ensuring
that the product has the right performance has the right
lifetime lifespan and if a product doesn't meet the requirement
it will not be solved it it doesn't work. So it's really a key point even
before we consider the economic aspect you need to meet
a certain number of criteria. Then we can look either at

life cycle costing for the economic aspect will just look a bit
at that and the social aspect with social LCA looking also at the structure
of salary and I say child labor or the training of women participate,
participation of women in the company and the question of equality which
are related also to products. But as we said LCA focus on
the environmental aspect and has this concept upstream and
procedure and really this this quantitative
assessment method are feeding for informing the different decision and
procedure. So let's look in more detail at this
six tools that we have here and let's define them a bit
in in further detail or seven tools that we have
a life cycle assessment. We've seen quantify a large
number of resource extraction and mission of substance and to estimate multiple environmental
impact associated with a given function. Substance flow analysis, quantify
the flow of environmental accumulation of a single substance usually or
a group of substance that we can have. So they focus they are they
are more narrow in that sense and and following the environment
following a certain region. This flow of given substance. Material flow analysis is basically doing the same but
with material and material can be raw material or
paper, glass, concrete, some basic material
used in the economy. Now on the quantitative also
side we have risk assessment and it studies the risk or
the probability of severe impact. And that could be an installation
like a nuclear power plant or usually with mostly used risk assessment
is for a chemical substance or eventually a group of substances that
we have and will go more in detail. Local environmental impact assessment,

a product of human activity or business. Water footprint, then is also a sectorial
sort of life cycle based analysis, which we look at the impact associated

water that could be water usage, water scarcity, we think,

## 02 Goal-And-Scope-Definition-Part-A

Goal and scope definition. Why on earth do we spend
an entire LCA phase, an entire one force of my LCA
just to scope the problem? That's because a problem which is well-defined
is half solved. It's really crucial, as we
saw in the popcorn example, that we define well the basis for comparison,
the metric used, the system boundaries, and that's why this goal and
scope definition is perhaps the most important phase and also sometimes the most
problematic phase in LCA. We start now and we'll spend some time on the goal
and scope definition to really define the
different element which serves the basis
then to calculate inventory of extraction
and impacts which are related to the
problem definition. Our learning objective
for today are to define the goal and
scope of an LCA and for this particular
lecture to identify the intended use and
user of the LCA, the decision context situation, and the intended audience. ISO 14044 give rule and say that in defining
the goal of an LCA, the following item shall be
unambiguously stated and when ISO said shall and not can that mean this
is a requirement. If you want your LCA to be ISO compliant
and ISO compatible, you need to do that, otherwise, you're
not. If these points are not explicitly in your
report you're out, reviewer will not give you the blessing for an
ISO compliance study. You need to define your
intended application, why you're carrying
out the study, who is the intended
audience to whom the results of the study are
intended to be communicated, and whether the
results are intended to be used in a
comparative assertion, meaning comparing
your product with another product explicitly
or even implicitly, and which is intended to be
disclosed to the public. Let's take the example of light bulbs and we will
define the scope and the goal of my LCA for typically comparing incandescent
light bulb with fluorescent or
an LED light bulb. Let's think what would be the objective and
reason for our study. Could be different things
in general for an LCA, could be product information, product development
within the company, defined policy and strategy at governmental or
business level or regulation at a
governmental level. In our case here, we can, for example, provide product information
to select what is the most suitable type of light bulb for a
given application. Typically our targeted
audience here will be consumers
whereas other LCA could be focused on the
governmental body or internal also for product development
inside the company. Then we need to
define the actors and the actors is a sponsor of the study, the
different authors. We'll see what is an advisory board and peer
reviewer in a minute. The more you involve independent
entities in your work, you will enhance the
credibility of your study. Let's look in further detail
about these actors here. The identity of the
main stakeholders and their addresses
should be provided. Let's say for sponsor, typically for this
light bulb study, we would have
consumer association. The author analyst,
of course, it's you, EHS672 consultant who will
become expert in a few weeks. That's your role as in your case study to
carry such a study. Optional advisory board. What is the role of
an advisory board? It's to provide
you the knowledge from different stakeholder
and ensure that all the hypotheses are setup in a fair way and often you
will involve people, for example, here
representative from the bulb manufacturer like astronomer Phillips
or General Electric. The electricity company would
be perhaps interesting, like DTE, the USEPA, or representative from an NGO like environmental defense or different NGO and if you're
a consumer association, you certainly will have someone representing the consumer
association in that. When you select these people, it's nice in fact to select
people who are potentially on the other side of the study. It's nice when you're
on the consumer side to have the bulb
manufacturer represented. Now, who do you choose in there? Two criteria to
choose the people. Knowledgeable, you want people who bring knowledge and
who bring insights. In particular, you're
not a specialist usually from the domain
when you do an LCA so you need to bring people who know about bulb and
will give you insight, will indicate where to
find some of the data, will help you for that. Second, you want them to
be open-minded experts. What I mean by that is you
don't want someone who has decided before the study
what the results should be. You need people who, looking at the evidences, looking at the science, can change their
mind while still representing a
certain stakeholder, and because if this person is well recognized
in his domain, it will give you credibility
and avoid that at the end, people say, they didn't consider one of the main
problem in our story. I have to say, in my experience, one of the first study I did was about rainwater
recuperation and we had a program officer
from the CCPA who was leading that and
a remarkable man, but his boss, at the start of our
study or before even we had signed the contract, basically said rainwater
recuperation is not useful and not applicable
really in Switzerland. We have enough water,
we don't need that. That was embarrassing
to do that. The way I got out
of that was to say, let's add to our
study a scenario of water saving techniques which would certainly or more
likely be of interest, whereas we also
identified, in some cases, rainwater could be of
interest in sub-sequence set. But it was really a
problem to have in fact, one of the person
sponsoring the study and we really had to be
careful to carry out a very independent
work in that case. The independence is
also ensured via optional peer reviewers
and these are really scientists,
independent LCA experts. Could be also from a company, but they are really knowledgeable
in LCA and they are chosen by the sponsor and the study author but should
be independent of you. That's not the people you
work on a weekly basis with. It's not people
within your business, it's people outside which
will give credibility.

## 01 Function-Functional-Unit-Part-A

we have seen with the popcorn example,

## 01 Building-Of-Product-System-And-Process-Tree-Part-A

LCA is keeping records of
a large number of flows. And there are different types of flow. And we need to structure
these thousands of flow and use them to first build
the product system and the process tree, so
how to deal with all this flow. We will learn it with
the funding learning objectives. We want to build the product system and
process tree. We want to define the product system on
a functional basis not surprisingly for LCA which is function based. We want to identify flow
intermediary between different economic process and
elementary from or to the environment. And then build this system process
tree composed of unit processes linked by these intermediary
flow between economic processes. Let's start by a few definitions. Product system is a collection
of unit processes which perform one or
more defined function. So a product system is in
fact defined by the product system here is a group of
unit processes defined by the product function that it serves. And it's characterized not
only by the final products, but really by the function
of these products. Okay, so ideally a product system
contains all the different processes that we have inside the system
that are required to achieve the function. And that means basically
that if I have included all processes here that serves
to serve this function. Okay, the input of the rest of
the economy is in fact zero because everything what is needed for
my product system is included here. We'll see in practice,
we have some exception. We don't want to work too long to that. So we'll have some rules for
good practice there. But ideally, basically, the only exchange with the rest of the
economy is the delivered product function. On the other hand, the product system as as a part of
the economy is in fact a machine or plant which is extracting
resources from the environment. And emitting, on the other hand,
residue along substances or pollutants to the environment to air,
to water, to soil or emitting noise also. We see that the environmental
here will be all marked. The flow from into the environment will
be all marking in yellow and here all the flow intermediary between different
economic processes are marked in blue. So, let's go in further detail and
look at one of these process which is basically
that the product system is disaggregated into
the series of unit process. So unit process is linked to
other unit process upstream via these intermediary flow or
flow downstream to another processes here via
another intermediary flow. So the intermediary flow are flows
that connect unit processes. The elementary flow are input
from the environment for each of these processes or
output to the environment which can occure in our system, okay? And presently we are building
the product system. So we focus mostly on intermediary flow. This is in the gold definition part. Okay, the inventory of the elementary
flow either as resources or as a mission is by definition
the quantification of all elementary flow crossing the system
boundary from and to the environment. And that will be treated
in the next chapter. So we park that and we think how
do we build our product system? So let's look at an example and
let's take a shoe example, here we have the shoe manufacturing
as our central unit process here. To build this shoe, we need some rubber. Okay that will be needed. We probably need if it's
a leather shoe some leather. Okay, and we might need some electricity
and some heat that we have here. The leather, this would be what we
call the tier one processes which are directly entering the manufacturer
of our shoe which is my main product and offering a pair of feet protected during
for example a year in the case of a shoe. So now the leather itself is
being produced by a cow and this cow is right on the farm. Okay, so we'll have another for
example, unit processes for the farm processing of the farm
production of my leather. And that will be here,
the tier two processes that will be used. And you have tier three

are needed by the farm at this level. So we build our products system

imagery flow to build from the mainstream manufacturing the tier one first
processes then the tier two etc. Each of these processes
itself can either extract flows from the environment like for
the first fade or the natural gas from ground for
electricity. Or more commonly in fact because
the extraction from the environment is usually done by mining operation. It will nearly all these unit processes
will have some emission to the air, to the water or to the soil that we can
see such as methane for the farm C02. For many of the processes PM 2.5 for
electricity production from coal for example and dye to fresh water
directly from my shoe manufacturing. These are called as we say
elementary flow in yellow and the intermediary flow which are used
to build our system are in blue here. On each of the unit process,
you could make a mass balance and an energy balance from all the inputs. Okay, and all the output. And this is very useful to
verify that the unit process and the global system respect
the conservation of energy and mass. It's not commonly done I
would say in all LCA or LCA database, but
that's an increasing tendency that we should in fact check our
balance that the sum of inputs correspond to the sum of outputs,
to check out our balance.

## 06 System-Boundaries-Part-A

Where shall we stop? When we speak of
system boundaries, should we include if we take
our example of popcorn, the machine who
manufactured the popcorn? What about the machine
who made the machine and the machine who made
the machine who made the machine who
manufactured popcorn? We don't have infinite time, we need to stop somewhere
in our assessment, so where to stop consistently and how to fix
these system boundaries. Our learning objective is to define consistent
system boundaries based on the product service and the function, and
more specifically, identify potential biases
in system boundary, determine rule for
good practice, and check whether
under which condition common processes to
different scenario can be excluded from
these boundaries. Let's take a counterexample. In the early 1990s, consultants worked for a very well-known international
fast food chain of restaurants and they compare a fast food with a
conventional restaurant. Basically, the consultant arrive with his results
and publishes, in fact, it was disclosed inside
the fast-food restaurant that the fast food requires
six time less energy, seven time less water, and surprisingly, five
times less waste. The last point was the most surprising from
my point of view. Looking at these results, we were starting investigating, but why do we get these results? Why is really the
question for science? When we don't understand
when we're surprised, we never let it go, we
always ask why, why, why, until we understand
and either we learn something new or
there was a problem. In this study, there was indeed some problems. It was a restaurant, so they had taken the boundary, the walls of my restaurant
as system boundary, and choosing geographical
rather than functional boundary does not necessarily
cover the same reality. We see that when we have here the different step
of food preparation, which are considered in the fast-food restaurant and in a conventional restaurant. If you take the wall
of the restaurant, what happens inside the
wall of the two here, the fast foods, and on the right, the
conventional restaurant. First, the preparation
of food and cooking is included in the
conventional restaurant, but this is excluded in my fast-food restaurant
because it's pre-prepared burger or
salad which are ready. The final cooking
is in both cases, but in addition to the cleaning, heating of the
restaurant itself, and the restaurant is
not really the same, there is not so much table
in a fast-food restaurant, here we have to also deal
with reusable dishes. We don't have here dishes, but we have packaging
and the packaging waste here can be not necessarily collected
inside my restaurant, so they might be
excluded, and secondly, the manufactured
of the packaging was not happening
in the restaurants, so it's also excluded. If we come back, the function of the fast food, in addition, is different because we have people in a conventional
restaurant will sit, will take time to speak whereas, in fast food, you don't offer
these secondary function. To compare rather the fast food, we should compare it with
another fast food for which we have reusable dishes
versus the takeaway. Now, about the waste, what is the difference
on the waste between the fast foods and the
conventional restaurant? First, the main waste stream in a normal
restaurant, what is it? It's the green waste, it's preparing my food. I have here losses, I have some bones
that are excluded and this compostable waste
are the main part, whereas it's packaging in
the case of the fast food. So very different waste, so taking just the
quantity as such doesn't qualify for an impact base
footprint of comparison. We need to account from which type of waste,
and in addition, as we said, the packaging
is not necessarily considered in my
fast-food restaurant. The preparation and the energy when preparing the burgers, salad, and all that, was also dis-considered in the fast food and not
in the conventional. Let's look at the system
boundary now for a proper study. Colleague from the ETH Zurich, the Switzerland
Institute of Technology, the Swiss MIT in Zurich, redid the same study, this time, according and
considering dishes, packaging, the food preparation, the dishwashing,
heating, lighting, and the waste treatment
equally in both scenarios. They were including what was happening in the pre-preparation of the food as well as what was happening within
the restaurant. Here the system boundary were counting for the same reality. Second, they compared
another fast food, one with reusable, this one is with reusable
dishes versus here, the takeaway fast food. They recounted also the
number of customer, in fact, the fast food customer
were overestimated or they hadn't taken really an average day in
the first study. We see that, in practice, the reusable dishes
was leading to a lower impact and one reason for it was a
reduction of transportation, the other reason was the reduction in the
secondary packaging, which is not completely
surprising in our case.


## 07 System-Boundaries-Part-B

Based on that, if we
want to avoid this bias, what are the rule for good practice in setting
our system boundary? The general rule is include all the necessary processes to assure the desired function, you want to have everything
which is necessary included. Second, the system
boundary should cover the same
functional reality, not geographical, not
company boundary, or business boundary, why? Because business boundary
will depend on what is outsourced to other company
versus what is produced, and when you compare
two companies, you cannot take the
whole of the company, you need to take the
functional reality, which is including the
whole supply chain of your company in both cases. Functional reality. Second, only processes
contributing to more than a certain
percentage are retained, or said as otherwise, you need to ensure that
all processes contributing to more than a certain
percentage are included. This percentage depend
on the level of detail of the study,
and why that? Because one of the
first study I made or I peer-reviewed in fact, was a study on flooring
from a Swedish company, and this flooring was
studied very much in detail with a thousand
different unit processes. That means that if you
would put a one percent, for example, cutoff and you
have such a level of detail, you are really in trouble if you start cutting everything
off or leaving out, which is all the processes
which are lower than a percent because you would
leave most processes. If we have, on the other hand, about 10 different
processes considered, one percent would be
goods as the basis because things
which contribute to lesser percent are small
compared to the other which, on average, would be of 5-20
or 30 percent as a whole. This cut-off really
depends on your own study. Second thing, the
cut-off criteria is really a minimum
inclusion requirement. We could formulate it as
we want to be sure that these processes are
included and are retained. Third rule is, when do we have identical processes in
a production system? Exactly the same processes, perhaps we could exclude between two scenario because we
have it in scenario 1, we have it in scenario 2, and if you're interested, one versus two, these
two things are equal. We could say, "I don't
need to study that, I know they are the same, I can disregard them." Let's look when we
can disregard them. We are saying that we can do it only if the intermediary flow affected by these processes
are strictly equal. Let's take an
example to do that, and I'll take the example
of my toothpaste. We'll compare three different
types of toothpaste. We have here self-standing
tube compared to packaged tube that you receive inside a cardboard altogether, and a dosing tube where you could take your
toothbrush and push it here and you would have

# Module 3: Life Cycle Inventory - Part 1

## 02 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Building-The-Lci-Part-A

Now that we have built our product system,
how can we study the flow which are crossing the system
boundary from the environment and to the environment and make
the inventory of these different flows. So this is the second phase of an LCA. Which look after the goal and
scope definition. Look at the inventory of extractions and
emission and and we are really interested to to
see when we compare scenario per functional unit, what we abstain there. So the learning objective in
building this life cycle inventory are to quantify the direct elementary
flow of each unit process, combine each unit process,
intermediary and elementary flow to obtain
aggregated inventory flows. And then we want a clear differentiation
that we understand if it's a direct flow or an aggregated flow per
functional unit which is accounting for the entire supply chain. In this second case,
let's start with a few definitions by definition the inventory of
elementary flow Is the list and amount of all the floor which
are crossing the system boundary from the environment for
the resources and to the environment for the emissions. So this is our green arrows
that we have here and we really have a list of at
least 400 substances depending on the database that are crossing
this boundary per functional unit. And this is what we aim
because we are aiming with LCA at the environmental impact. So that's what we want to assess. Let's take an example
of shoe manufacturing. Okay. And we want when we
determine the elementary for shoe manufacturing to take not only
the direct emission to air but also we know that for shoe manufacturing
we need, for example some rubber, we need some leather and we need some
electricity for the manufacturing. This is a tier one, tier two. We need a farm because leather
comes from comes from a cow and you need to grow your cow and
that means you need fertilizer. And so
we have the the the entire process and emission can occure at each of this
unit process that we have here. So if we want the total
aggregated of all the C02 emissions, we need to move up and
down the process tree and obtain all these emissions, but
we want them per functional unit. Okay.
That so that we can sum them consistently here. So it means taking into account of C02 emission not only during
shoe manufacturing, but during all these different processes
that we have in the process tree.


## 03 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Building-The-Lci-Part-B

How do we do that? We want to use a
step-wise procedure. This step-wise procedure
works as follow, and we're going to illustrate
it with a case of aluminum. This is an aluminum tube which was used in fact
for Delta plane. When I did my first internship
nearly 40 years ago and when the person doing
that had some extra one. I'm using them for

for transportation, especially air transportation, everything in a plane is made

and the emission for one-kilo aluminum
liquid that we produce? Let's take the example
of heat waste. It's an emission of heat and emission of megajoule
to the environment, waste heat to the environment. First, we need to find
the direct emission and extraction factors
of each process per kilo for each process. The megajoule heat waste

per functional unit. This is what we want in megajoule heat waste

contribution of each of these unit processes to the

of heat is large, is 56 megajoule

our process system and we know the quantity

## 04 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Building-The-Lci-Part-C

The ecoinvent database provide
these two types of data. It provides unit process level. These are processes which
are called with U, which have the detail of direct elementary flow
and intermediary. It means with any data
you always account for the 4,000 other
processes to get it. It's complicated, but you
have a high level of detail, which is really nice
when you want to just modify one of these process. You just modify
exactly what you want and you can rerun it
and get your results. The second level, which is
easier to use and I recommend, I would say that you use the system level by default when you will
work on SimaPro. It's the aggregated
elementary flow that you have for a given product summed up over the entire supply chain. No intermediary flow here, only total elementary flow
per functional unit or per kilo of the commodity
that we are defining. Many other databases don't
have the same resolution, only offer aggregated flow, which is problematic because you cannot modify them easily. So you have to ask the
people who've done the data to modify them, which some company like to keep their customer
dependent on them, but personally and in
our quantities company, we are trying to affect
our customer independence. They will need us because
we didn't need to be always cutting edge and
we'll have the next ID. Such aggregate
inventory flow for different processes can
be directly used to build the inventory of new
products and we see with a car example how once you have these
aggregated system level flow, you can use them
relatively easy, even Excel spreadsheet to build the impact of a given
product so in summary, the inventory phase
of the LCA determine the elementary flow or emission and extraction
per functional unit. Accounting for the
entire processes which contribute to
the project function. The inventory is
calculating by combining the intermediary flow
per functional unit and the elementary flow per unit of the same unit process to get the total per functional
unit at each level. So it's important that we don't mix the intermediary direct and the aggregated
elementary flow over our products system. Finally, the good news is that we have a lot
of inventory data. The bad news is correcting
even one process for inventory data on
the intermediary and elementary flow is
really hard work. So you need direct
contact with company, or you need to go
in the literature, it's pretty hard work. But the beauty is we have a lot of processes
which are existing. We can rely on that and
just do it for what is needed as a complement
to what we already have.


## 01 Primary-Energy-And-Co2-Emissions-From-Processes-Materials-Part-A

Now that we know
how to aggregate the different
elementary flow across the entire supply chain and
get aggregated results, I would say cradle to gate
for different material, it's very interesting to
compare the primary energy we are getting or
the CO_2 emission. But to do that, we first need to define well, what type of energy
because there are several term which are used
for describing the energy. We want to define as a
learning objective primary, final, and useful energy. Second, we will then compare aggregated processes
for primary energy for various materials
and processes. Let's look at this definition. Primary energy is
defined as the energy contained in the energy carrier at the point of extraction. It's the total energy
you extract from the environment and that will include the upstream
energy usage that you need to
do the extraction, to do the refinery, the preparation, and to
distribute all that. You need to extract
all that so that you have the final
energy which is delivered to the consumer or purchased by the consumers if we take his or her
point of view. The final energy is what is consumed whereas the
primary energy is what needs to be extracted to deliver this energy consumed. The useful energy
is the portion of the final energy
which is actually delivered inside the
house for example, or available after
final conversion for the respective
use of the consumer. Let's look at an example
to understand that. Let's take natural gas first. We have here some
gas and I buy one megajoule final which
is at my gas meter. First, what's happening
when you have a heating, usually you have a
small stack on the roof and you in fact are
ejecting some heat. The efficiency will be
a key parameter here which will relate the final

## 01 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Databases-Part-A

Where to find consistent and
high quality data. How how can we recognize what data, good quality and
where the place to find them. This is our goal for today. And the learner objective is
to describe the different life cycle inventory database
which are available. It's to illustrate the data
format of one specific and mostly used database,
the ecoinvent database. The database is to recognize
different types of data and energies based inventory flows and
use them adequately. And finally, to identify source for
direct data, life cycle inventory, data collection,
LCI for life cycle inventory. Good.
So, first in the life cycle inventory database, we have two types of modeling
which are answering different questions. The first time is the attributional LCA. Where we look at a product and
we look at what are the share of the activity
in the world that have really contributed to that product. So can be attributed,
allocated to the given products. What is the average share of the impact
that this product is responsible of? And for this we use typically
average electricity mix that we consider because if
this process use electricity, we assume that it will
use the same share of electricity as the other in the same mix. Making with the same proportion between
nuclear gas power plants or hydro that we get our coal power plant that we
get this average sort of contribution. The other approach is
called consequential. And in consequential approach, you want to study what is
expected to change, okay? In the environmental impact
when suddenly you add a product to the present economy, okay? So, when producing consuming and disposing
the product, what are the change? So you want to identify marginal change, here marginal is a key word. And it means you will look, for example, if I add a certain
electricity consumption, what is the likely additional
technology which will either for example, in the growing market is likely
that the new plants are gas power plant. So you will use only electricity from gas. Or if you are in a decreasing market, it's likely that coal power plants
are the ones which are fazed off and which will be considered for
the marginal change here. You have to be careful when you
do consequential because you have the risk that you are only
taking marginal change. But within the time of
your product system, if you study for
example electricity production or energy production,
a power plant will stay 40 years. During 40 years, it's unlikely
that the change are marginal. So personally, I'm a bit more tendentially
using by default attributional. But I have colleagues who are very
strongly in favor of consequential but it really depends on
the type of question and I would say the timescale of
the product you are looking. If you're just looking
at one point in time or if you're looking on the longer
term of the decision. So now, where do you find

## 01 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Special-Topics-Part-A-Allocation

How do we handle when
a process is producing simultaneously different core-products. How to separate and attribute part
of the emission to one product and the other part to the second one,
that's what we are going to see. And our objective is how to handle
core-product in life cycle assessment. And we will identify suited
allocation method to the problem and rules for
good versus inappropriate practice. So let's look at the allocation
between two products and let's take an example to decide
how to separate two products. So let's take a wheat crop. And this wheat crop, you have different
operations like the plowing and harvesting and all this operation and at the end you have your wheat
that you were intending to obtain. But in addition you also have some
straw that you have produced. And the question is the raw
material extraction for the detail of the tractor for example or
the emission from that same tractor, how to separate them and allocated partly
to the straw and partly to the wheat, because in general we are interested in
the wheat for example for bread making. So to do that,
we need an allocation procedure and keyword here is causality. We only will accept to do it if there
is a causality relationship and we will use method based on causality. Let's look at what 14 or 44 is proposing as a preference order,
okay? So the allocation method
can be applied and each of these allocation only
if they fulfill the respective condition of use and
have this causality principle and this should be done in
the following order of preference. First we propose to do process separation. If it is possible to disassociate
the different production system. So let's take our straw and our wheat. So the straw here and
the wheat product A, okay? And let's think of plowing our field,
okay? Does plowing belong to wheat or to straw? We cannot separate that
we need the plowing, we need the sowing of the wheat and
this will both produce wheat and straw. So this approach is not
applicable in this situation but it could be partly apply
when we think that for the straw bales and
the baling here of my straw. This really only belong to B. So from the point of harvest
everything which is downstream from that should be attributed
either to the straw or to the wheat, but
not to both of them in that case, okay? But not really possible to
apply fully in that case. The second method to apply in
order of preference is what is called system expansion. The idea is to say,
my core product B, okay, is in fact substituting another product in
the economy that we don't need to produce. Let's call it product product B prime,
which has a similar function but not necessarily exactly the same or
not the same way to produce. Let's take an example,
if you're in Denmark and you produce straw,
straw is often used for producing heat. And if you produce heat here, okay, you may be substituting heat
production from natural gas. Okay, so now the idea is to say
we can subtract to process A and B, the emission associated
with the heat of natural gas that we haven't avoided burden
sort of bonus for that. And so we will say that the emission of product A equal to the emission of product (A + B)- the emission of product B prime, okay? And that's away which is
relatively rigorous but and there is a bad this is only valid
if B is indeed substituting B prime. So if the substituted core product
is fully defined known and it really happens okay,
but if it's the case, this is this is really a good procedure. The third possibility is to
do physical allocation and for example, on the basis of mass or
energy content, but this is only valid if there is
a causality between the mass and the amount of each of these
products of the emission associated with each
of these two products. So if we take the case of the wheat and
the straw, we could think that if you feed both
the wheat and the straw to a cow and that can happen in in in in
some cases not very common, but it happens okay,
you could take X as typically the nutritional content
of the of the feet, Okay. Or the the energy in the feet and allocate proportionally to the energy
produced via the wheat and the energy produce and
fed to the cow via the stroke. But now if wheat is used for bread making,
we are not eating the stroke. So we cannot use the energy content
as a basis for allocating this. So in that case we we were not
going to use this approach and we jump on the fourth approach
which is generally nearly always applicable is a financial and
economic allocation. Okay.
And here the economic allocation is a measure of the incentive for producing. And so we will assess the value of process
a product A the value of product B. And we reallocate
proportionally to these values. two points linked to that some people

## 02 Life-Cycle-Inventory-Special-Topics-Part-B-Input-Output

We know that getting new data for life cycle
inventory is hot, so could we benefit
from existing data to get an easy way to obtain the first order of magnitude
for many different product? This is exactly
what input-output LCA economic-based
LCA is offering. The learning objectives are to introduce the economic-based
input-output LCA and apply this
economic input-output LCA to the hand-dryer
example to show you how you can perform
quickly an LCA on this basis. Process LCA, we know, is based on technical
coefficient and detailed process modeling
for core processes. If we take the
example of aluminum, one of the main physical
flow for aluminum are the kilowatt-hour electricity
used per kilogram aluminum. What we're basically
doing in process LCA is multiplying
these intermediary physical flow by an
elementary flow of CO_2, for example, per physical units, so in kilo CO_2 per
kilowatt-hour electricity. When we multiply that, the kilowatt-hour electricity
goes away and we get the kilo CO_2 per kilo aluminum. That will be one of the
inventory flow that we have. Now, economic
input-output-based LCA rely on data which are coming on the spending
of each sector. We say, for example, for one unit output
of this sector here, this sector will spend money
in another two sectors. For example, this
sector at tier 1, will then spend amount of money in other sector at tier 2. We continue like
that up to infinity. The beauty is any industry
from a sector is defacto reporting to the Bureau
of Economic Analysis in the US how much spending
they make in 400 sectors. We can start building
this network for 400 different types of products or commodities,
or sectors. We can have either
commodity or sector based. How does it work? Instead of an intermediary
physical flow, we have now an intermediary
economic flow, which are the dollars
spent on buying electricity per dollar
aluminum output or aluminum produce. What we need is determine
elementary flow per dollar, per economic units
in, for example, kilo CO_2 per
dollar electricity, to multiply that, and then the dollar
electricity go away, and we get kilo CO_2
per dollar aluminum, which will be our
new inventory flow. If we multiply that
by the number of dollar aluminum per
functional unit, we will get the kilo CO_2
per functional unit. The same way that here, we were multiplying by the kilo aluminum
per functional unit, and we were getting
the same kilo CO_2 per functional unit
in both approaches. Similar approaches, how do we get the kilo CO_2 per
dollar electricity? We, in fact, take the
overall electricity sector, look at how many dollar output
we have from electricity, what is the total CO_2 emission from the electricity sector, and do the relative ratio
of it to calculate this. Let's take an example and use a small tool which
